‚öôÔ∏è üåç New Ventures Systems

   * FTCP (PCS): We switched 70% of the traffic to live on FTCP cluster . We identified consumer lag issues, so we manually scaled the consumer to zero and are investigating. Once resolved, we‚Äôll resume the rollout with a gradual traffic increase to FTCP.

   * RFC ‚Äì Profile Service v2: Pending final approval from the RTE tribe.

   * ADR ‚Äì Deprecating subscribable-addons-bff: The purpose of this ADR is to define how we handle customer communication when subscribing to addons. Currently, this is managed by the [subscribable-addons-bff] service, where the frontend generates the event and sends it alongside the subscription request. With the broader adoption, and the launch of the GraphQL API, the proposal is to move this responsibility to the backend via NV-CRM events. A POC confirmed data usability, and we‚Äôre investigating the scope of FE, BE, and CRM changes.

                     * New Ventures - Himash

üê∂ Pet Food

                     * This week the team continued to focus on the Air Dried cadence test. This initiative aims to convert air dried users into a lower cadence in order to reduce the price shock when they reach checkout. 

                     * On Wednesday we also deactivated all discontinued SKUs (Half of Fresh plan and discontinued calories).

                     * The team also started preliminary work for our next fresh recipe launch (Pork Stew with Butternut Squash) coming on Tuesday (June 10th).

This will enable users to leverage modularity, collections, add-ons, and surcharges in pre-checkout selection while also storing selected cuts for future use.

üë™ Team and People Updates

                                                            * New Ventures - Himash

üê∂ Pet Food

                                                            * We are continuing working on the simplify rescheduling initiative. This week we were focused on creating the carousel and setting up the selection logic.

                                                            * The quick win for this sprint is making add-ons subscribable by default. TPT customers will now be able to add add-ons to their subscription plans instead of just their next box, aligning with the standard practice among leading pet food companies. This change aims to improve the add-on take rate.

                                                            * We discovered that after UPM integration, the acceptance rate of PayPal transactions has dropped from 95% to 37%. During investigation it turned out that the UPM component was attached to a HF DE PayPal account, which resulted in customers using paypal being declined after cut-off due to BILLING_AGREEMENT_NOT_FOUND. Payments team has enabled shared billing agreements between KN and DE and after the Thursday cut-off 92% of Paypal transactions are successful.

                                                            * An update to calories calculation was released on live o/

üíª Other Tech Initiatives

                                                            * Creating configuration projects in Web was not straightforward, developers had deal with providers and server middlewares, and forgetting to do either of these things could lead to performance issues or live incidents. A couple of days ago we released a new additional way of creating configuration projects for small config objects, that only export a React hook to access the config, without dealing with providers and server middlewares. More info in this announcement.

üíª Other Tech Notes

This week, web-foundation with our assistance investigated an incident (for 2.5-days üòµ‚Äçüí´) - #in-31817-2404 Some customers would experience 500 errors every time we do a deployment. It was present probably forever and increased on March 21st. The amount was not too crazy (about 50-200 cases per deployment depending on the traffic across all web-repo requests), yet it might have affected you - you might have experienced this issue, saw customer complaints, or maybe adjusted your SLOs to match this ‚Äúaccepted failure rate‚Äù. Letting you know that now it is resolved!

We couldn‚Äôt be more excited to be working with each and every team member in 2024. We have got ambitious, exciting, and cool plans for 2024. If you want to understand where roadmaps and team setups are coming from, you are invited to go through them in the 2024 HelloTech Yearly Plan - TAM Expansion Alliance Final and get pumped!





Throughout the coming weeks, we work mindfully on transitions, handovers, on and off boarding sessions. These will hopefully set us up as a consolidated organization by February 1st. We‚Äôre fully dedicated to support everyone in case of a transition and beyond. We are always here to talk, so please reach out. The doors are always open as we literally have no doors! üòÄ





Have a great year ahead, 

Tobias & Nikita

2023-W51 (Dec 22)

This is the last email of the year and instead of team updates please find a message from our tribe leadership below ‚ù§Ô∏è üéÅ üéÜ

=====

A quick interception by Max:

                                                                        * Dec 25-26th and Jan 1st are public holidays! üéÑ

                                                                        * Engineers on-call: week 52 - Vini, week 01 - Bolo! (good luck, guys ü§û)

                                                                        * I wish all the best in 2024 and forecasting it a blasting year: all the bugs will be fixed, OKR achieved, migrations and refacroting completed, no single critical will happen and everyone will receive at least 500% salary raise!!!

(please consider - the forecast might be not very accurate)

======

Dear Team, we wanted to provide you with a personalized and heartfelt message from ourselves and this is the best that we came up with: 

  



But in all seriousness‚Ä¶

Dear Team,

Thank you for all your passion and contribution in 2023. You have been an amazing team. We, personally, have enjoyed every moment of working together with you - no matter if it was laughing, discussing, planning, executing, struggling, or winning. For us as New Ventures, it was an incredibly successful year. Simply put - you absolutely rock. üßë‚Äçüé§

It is always a balancing act when calling out achievements. Too easy to miss something or suggest an order. So, let us go by the alphabet and share some highlights from our perspective. (Of course, there were many more!)

B2B: You‚Äôve ramped up an entire new business from scratch and even convinced our Management Board that B2B does work. All the challenges you took from navigating a lot of unknowns, ambiguity, and a new tech stack is nothing short of phenomenal. You‚Äôve created partnerships all along. Bringing a brand new vertical from zero to hero is something to be proud of, especially given that the impact of this work is now becoming visible externally from HelloFresh. As Monasin put it aptly during our AHM - it‚Äôs the first time in HelloFresh history that a commercial team admits openly ‚Äúwe need to catch up‚Äù. 

Good Chop: Tripling the size of your business, doesn‚Äôt come for granted. Though you did! Your fast pace, adaptiveness, and dedication made Good Chop into a brand which is larger than many of our international markets. You did this while tackling significant macro headwinds (inflation and customer behaviour changes) in a vertical, which is unknown to most customers. Moreover, the Good Chop brand and its technology have consistently been the innovation driver for the whole group with HelloFresh. What you have built has heavily influenced many global concepts, experiments, and experiences.

Pet Food: Launching a new brand (another new vertical!) and making it the fastest-growing new vertical in HelloFresh history is something that we didn‚Äôt dare to dream of when joining HelloFresh. Your contributions have played a pivotal role in positioning us in this market. and making a positive impact on pet nutrition in the US. That gave us strong conviction that you have the superpower to scale the business into new heights. Way to go!

X-Brand: The work done on X-Brand has been groundbreaking. It's a testament to your ability to push boundaries and embrace challenges. X-Brand is more than just a one-time project; it represents our collective force to pioneer and innovate and the first foray into moving HelloFresh from a mealkit business to a truly comprehensive food service provider for the households worldwide. 

After all, we know that it was not only easy-peasy. As a team, we reasonably debated green bananas, challenging deadlines, coming to the office, desk availability, and more. We highly appreciate the openness, controversies and candor each one of you has brought to the table. We felt that we matured as a team in several regards. We hope you feel so, too. Most of you joined us in 2021 or 2022. We went into 2023 with a shift from New Brands Retention to New Ventures as well as with some question marks. Now, it is one year later. We seem to have found a rhythm and better feeling of how to organize ourselves.

We are excited to onboard together with you into 2024. We wish you a wonderful Christmas time and a Happy New Year.

Nikita & Tobias

‚öôÔ∏è Backend

                                                                           * This week we are still being blocked from NV-CRM going live as the events are not showing up on Salesforce yet. Commstech is troubleshotting it together with us

üíª Other Tech Initiatives

                                                                           * The legacy Whitelabel emotion-js Theme has been migrated to TypeScript. In the migration process we discovered and fixed more than 50 small errors caused by components using un-existing theme styles. Having the theme implemented with TS will give us more safety when migrating components to Zest and removing unused theme styles, and it‚Äôs one of the prerequisites for the eventual extraction of this theme out of the whitelabel space (breaking down the monolith!)

                                                                           * We‚Äôve started a learning program called Tech Toaster: Frontend Career Development (details). It's a 6-session journey where experienced colleagues will share insights and mental models to empower Frontend engineers. This will include risk management, cross-team collaboration, interpreting our career framework as a Frontend Engineer, and much more!

The 3 alerts are linked to the New Brands Web OpsGenie team, and will be updated accordingly after the on-call split.

ü•© Good Chop

‚öôÔ∏è Backend

                                                                                                * Although still in the research and planning phase, we have started working on the new CRM service. 

                                                                                                * Why build a new service? 

                                                                                                * The NV brands are constantly coming up against CRM issues involving missing or incorrect data. The main reason is because these brands have some unique data and features (delivery cadence, pet profile, trial box etc.) and these aren‚Äôt factored into the existing HF CRM events. Also it‚Äôs not recommended to fix these issues in the original CRM events since these events serve all brands inside the company and they‚Äôre meant to be generic. So instead we want to build a new service that triggers events with the specific data that the NV brands want

                                                                                                * We recently found out that several teams throughout HF (inside and outside of TAM) are interested in building some sort of profile service that‚Äôs meant to extend the customer in some way (E.g. a customer taste profile). Since we already have a similar use case implemented in TPT (nutritional-profile-service) we‚Äôve reached out to try to come to one unified solution that everyone can use. This is still in the brainstorming phase but the goal is to allow us to collect more information about the customer beyond what is currently available in the customer object, and different services can get this information in order to improve the customer experience (e.g. personalize their recommendations)

üíº Multi-Venture Platform

                                                                                                * Cigna project:

                                                                                                * The team is ready to launch the Cigna community on July 17th üöÄ and offer healthy meals to 350k clients of Cigna company HF US, Factor, and GreenChef US üéÅ

                                                                                                * A demo video can be found here.

                                                                                                * The team has officially taken ownership of the Community Discount Service (CMDS).

                                                                                                * B2B boxes are now officially available in the ODL pipelines as of Thursday, July 6th! üöÄThis will help reduce the logistics and fulfillment issues that have occurred the last few weeks.

                                                                                                * Kudos to our partners from Katana and USBTA teams üëè

                                                                                                * Details:

                                                                                                * B2B orders were previously located in a separate ODL file, but will now be directly incorporated into the Factor ODL files ingested into the Snowflake/CDP/Photon ODL Pipelines.

                                                                                                * Availability of B2B boxes in our database tables is critical for downstream teams to monitor and report on the new process.

                                                                                                * B2B and non-B2B orders will be merged in the Katana process AFTER the PRIO ODL but BEFORE the ADL. The merged file will be what's available in our tables and what's sent to ScanData.

                                                                                                * B2B boxes can be distinguished by their DU_ID -- each record will have a designated 'B' at the end (ex. F10492B).

üíª Other Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                * A big maintenance problem we‚Äôve had for a long time is the duplication of our whitelabel CloudFlare page rules. TAM currently supports 13 different website domains, each one with their own set of Page Rules that implement CDN caching, redirections and proxies to S3. Adding a rule to start caching a new page requires modifying 13 different files. To solve this problem, we created a `whitelabel-rules` terraform module that contains all shared CloudFlare configuration. While moving CDN configs from each domain module to the shared module, we are also migrating Page Rules to their new and improved version: Cache Rules.

üíª Other Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                * Fresh from the oven ü•ñ! Since yesterday morning we have CDN caching metrics of our HTML pages in all our frontend HoneyComb traces. Before, the only way to get some basic cache metrics was by going to CloudFlare‚Äôs dashboard and doing some low level queries. With the new HoneyComb data you can calculate cache hit ratio of any web page, and compare performance metrics between cached vs non-cached response - spoiler alert, the difference is huge! Below is the LCP of the whitelabel Plans page, where you can see the non-cached responses are 3 times slower than the cached ones. With this data, we hope that teams will take a look at their caching metrics and implement improvements.

üíª Other Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                         * When creating configuration projects using `@/libs/config` it‚Äôs very important to load the config‚Äôs server middleware in the pages that use the config. By doing this, the config for the current country and environment is resolved in the server side instead of dynamically in the client side. Client-side dynamic resolutions of configs is bad because not only the React app will need to load a JS chunk that has the entire config object, the Config Provider will delay the rendering of its children to the client side, making the user experience much slower. We found more than 20 WL config projects that are not being correctly resolved on the server side: https://ui.honeycomb.io/hellofresh/datasets/traces-frontend-live/result/75wJVMh4EGS. We ask all teams to take a look at this list and fix them ASAP.

üíª Other Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                               * The Unification team released a couple of unified components in the last few days in some mealkit countries: the checkout header and the checkout order summary. The next step is to start unifying the Sign Up page (see RFC)

                                                                                                               * In the last months we‚Äôve been having some noise in Sentry related to a weird problem that sometimes happens when Google Translate is used in some versions of Chrome, breaking React‚Äôs virtual DOM (they wrapped translated content with <font> tags). This problem was mostly happening on our Image component, since NextJS is wrapping images with span tags. This week we wrapped the NextJS image component with an ErrorBoundary to reduce the blast radius of the problem, and to reduce the Sentry log level to warning. The root problem will be fixed with the NextJS 13 upgrade, but in the meantime we wanted to reduce the noise caused by it.

üéÑüéÑüéÑ End-of-year NoteüéÑüéÑüéÑ





Big congratulations everyone for making this year unbelievably successful! Thanks to your hard work, dedication and passion, this year has been a resounding success. The tribe achieved the lion‚Äôs share (89%!) of its OKRs with flying colors, innovated both within our domains (e.g. New Recipe Cards) but, crucially, also drove innovation across HelloTech (Staging for Non-Techies). If we look back at where the tribe started it would be hard to imagine how successful Good Chop would be by now, how easy to use and engaging would EveryPlate and Factor become for their customers. Even at the very last days of 2022 you managed to deliver huge improvements for our customers - Trial Box and Subscribable Add-ons. 





Thanks to your efforts we go into 2023 with incredibly ambitious goals that we know we will be able to achieve! We look forward to working side by side with you in the coming year and wish you Happy Holidays and a Happy New Year! 





Thank you,

Tobias & Nikita

üç± Unified Mealkits

                                                                                                                        * One of the first sections we want to unify is the Testimonials/Trustpilot reviews. Between HF and all whitelabel countries, we have 4 different components showing customer reviews, using 3 different data sources (RCS, Contentful & Trustpilot). Not only would we like to reduce the number of components we used for this purpose, we also want to have a single data source. We documented the different testimonial components we currently have, and assessed pros and cons of removing their content from Contentful/RCS and using the Trustpilot API instead (link to doc).

                                                                                                                        * We created our first pull request refactoring a HF Plans page component, replacing RCS toggles with the config lib, replacing usages of legacy APIs and migrating the files to Typescript - this is the type of improvements we want to do on the entire page, to modularize each section making it reusable to all brands.

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                        * As an additional part of the Testing-Library Migration Tech Initiative, we have been working on collecting coverage from our unit and integration tests. The goal is looking for potential use cases we are still covering. After some initial work and POC, we are finally collecting it everyday inside one of web-infra‚Äôs cronjob. This data is currently available on a simple chart including every team with your own coverage percentage. The next step is creating more visualised data filtered only by the New Brands teams! Big kudos to Desi, Max, Mateusz, Bolo and the frontend infra folks!

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                        * We presented and discussed our QQR Q1/2022 goals in the tribe on Thursday: (1) Double down on business SLOs, (2) Definition of failure. Two takeaways from the discussion:

                                                                                                                        * We need to gain more experience to build Visual Tests in a non-flaky way, i.e. get a better feeling for granularity and deviation tolerance.

                                                                                                                        * ‚ÄúIncident‚Äù is a process for escalation and getting attention. Definition of ‚Äúcritical‚Äù is a framework to allow everyone independently to decide on the urgency of an issue. When being on the fence, assume the higher criticality. There is nothing wrong with triggering a critical and concluding in hindsight that it was not critical. Failures, criticals, incidents, and post-mortems are a great source for learning, let‚Äôs embrace them, even if it feels sometimes like a ‚Äúlittle too much process‚Äù.

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                              * As a company we move away from Concourse to GitHub Actions. We own four remaining Concourse pipelines to be migrated. nutrition-cards-cron is probably the most compex one. Fede is looking for people to pair. This is a chance to learn something and help us get rid of legacy.

                                                                                                                              * A recurrent problem we have is that HelloTech doesn‚Äôt have a good way to store technical metrics that could be used to track the progress of migrations or other technical initiatives in an automated way. Last month, Fede described this problem and proposed a solution in this RFC. This week a first proof of concept was implemented: a web toolbox command that exports pull request metadata from Github to a Google Spreadsheet. We will be implementing another toolbox command to do something similar with JIRA tickets, which we will eventually use to calculate Change Failure Rate by counting JIRA bug tickets and merged Pull Requests. This kind of tools open up a lot of possibilities, if you have an idea of something we could start tracking please let Fede know!

üí• Critical Incidents

                                                                                                                              * On Monday evening an incident was triggered after we got several complaints from users that were unable to unsubscribe from our email newsletters. The problem was fixed after reverting a Soft Login change introduced the previous week. We already created a HoneyComb alert that would trigger when the number of newsletter un-subscriptions is below an abnormal threshold, and we will be implementing E2E tests to prevent this issue from happening again. More info on the incident‚Äôs channel: #in-17756-2202

                                                                                                                              * Yesterday evening an incident was triggered after GreenChef US customer care team realised that they were getting chat messages from GreenChef UK customers. Then more GreenChef US-UK mixups were detected. The issue was caused by a GTM refactoring done by the frontend infra team, that mixed the GTM ids of both countries. A hotfix was released around 3am fixing the problem. More info on the incident‚Äôs channel: #in-17773-2202

üí• Critical Incident

On Monday morning we triggered a Critical Incident after seeing several problems with the Endless Pause endpoint used by Good Chop. After some investigation, we found that the problem was introduced on Thursday evening with some changes to the authentication library in frontend infra. The issue was fixed on Monday noon, and after that we had to manually fix the data of ~250 customers that had a weekly subscription due to this issue. There will be two post-mortems written, one by Frontend Infra and one by Vini‚Äôs team.

                                                                                                                              * Fab4+ metrics exist now on Squad Level. For now, please discuss the Fab4+ metrics with your Squad Lead.

                                                                                                                              * The ‚Äã‚ÄãData Access in the Server Side RFC is finally complete, and the proposed solution has been implemented as a proof of        concept. Last week the background-data-refreshing was first used for HF Applanga translations, and after a few days without problems we rolled it out for RCS and Optimizely datafile. This morning during Chapter Day we had a session to explain how this solution works, and implemented it for Presets, Products and Contentful (whitelabel only). We expect to see an increase of service availability (less alerts) and a decrease in latency during off-hours (when people are mostly asleep, and cache hit ratio is normally down).

                                                                                                                              * The Enhance e2e tests initiative has been marked as complete after a lot of hard work (shoutout to Max and Bolo for leading it!). The last milestone was to write a document explaining our QA Strategy and how we do E2E testing with Cypress. Please check them out!

                                                                                                                              * We launched today the meal choice experience survey on FJ, will rollout to the rest of the countries after the holiday

üíª Tech Initiatives

This week we completed two big tech initiatives:

                                                                                                                              * Terminate whitelabel-web service: after removing/migrated all endpoints in whitelabel-web, we were finally able to deprecate and terminate the service. We still have the whitelabel-web repo because there are a couple of concourse jobs in there that are still being used by us.

                                                                                                                              * Unbind dependencies: one big issue we started having after migrating to frontend infra is that our code had a lot of bad internal dependencies. This was causing some circular dependencies between packages, and it was slowing down the CI by running E2E tests that were not really needed. After extracting code to new libraries and removing some problematic import-export root files (icons, common components, store) we consider this initiative done. I will be sharing more info on this topic once we are all back in January.

üõí M&M

                                                                                                                              * The premium recipes price test that we did on CK was recently completed and it had interesting results. Surcharge revenue (main metric for the test) increased for the variation where we increased $1 per serving, but further investigation showed that add-ons revenue and seamless revenue increased for the variation where we decreased $1 per serving, so they cancel each other out in the end.. As a next step we are awaiting feedback from Chefs Plate, as which version to roll out is highly depending on the local team‚Äôs strategy (i.e. whether to push for premium recipes or add-ons & seamless).

üí• Critical Incident

This morning at 5am we had a critical incident in our whitelabel web pages, caused by a latency spike in RCS. Even though the issue fixed itself after a few minutes, we still need to work on improving our resiliency on different levels: fallback RCS data when API is down (or any other type of data used by server), and improving CDN caching to return stale HTML pages when the service is down (currently implemented in most of our pages, but we still miss a couple of important ones). Here‚Äôs the link to the incident‚Äôs post mortem.

üíª Tech Initiatives

The Engagement team removed all API calls to the second-voucher endpoint and M&M migrated the `/recipe-rating` endpoint to NextJS (kudos to Suzi, Guhan, Mateusz and Max for this complex migration!).

Quarterly Quality Review (QQR)

Last Friday we had our QQR for Q3 where Tobias, Ahmed and Alex presented to Yoav, Davor and Monasin what we achieved during the last quarter and some of the topics we want to tackle on Q4. If you haven‚Äôt done so yet, I recommend looking at the slides. In the next few weeks we will be discussing the goals and action items for Q4.

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                              * This week we finished moving all our static config files from the whitelabel space, to a new library called ‚Äúwhitelabel-static-config‚Äù. This is part of a bigger initiative to untangle the dependency between our packages. As part of this initiative, we also found some unused legacy code from our old routing system that was causing all whitelabel pages to indirectly depend on the rest of the pages. By removing this code, a change on a single page should only trigger the cypress tests on that page only, instead of running all our tests.

                                                                                                                              * After A-DOS worked on removing some 3rd party dependencies in our react-native app and converted the distributable file(s) from APK to AAB, he wrote a nice post in our HelloTech engineering blog.

We are going to discuss in sprint plannings how to prioritize the tickets related to the features we own in New Brands Retention.

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                              * I wrote an RFC to formalize the discussions we‚Äôve been having about adding some responsibilities to the on-call engineers. Please read it and give your thoughts!

                                                                                                                              * Last week we found a big performance issue when running whitelabel on the new infra due to how NextJS works during page transitions. Every NextJS page component can define a list of endpoints that should be fetched, so the page can use the returned data to render the HTML. Every one of our pages need contentful data, products, preferences, optimizely datafile and RCS. The problem we had was that when going from one page to another, NextJS was fetching all this data over and over again making the page transition very slow. Yesterday we were able to merge a proof of concept fix, and this morning we released the fix to all whitelabel pages in web infra.

                                                                                                                              * Now that there are no outstanding issues that can block the migration, we will start testing our New Brands in the web infra. Of course we need to verify that all user flows are working as expected, but since our TestCafe tests are all passing against the web infra, we will need to pay extra attention to infrastructure topics that are not covered by our e2e tests. I created a list with these points, feel free to add anything that I might have missed. https://hellofresh.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SC/pages/2936569923/Testing+Plan

                                                                                                                              * The first version of HelloDev was released by Platform. It is HelloTech‚Äôs central Developer Productivity tool for the future. More infos to come. You may have a first look and click around (VPN needed). It is based on Spotify‚Äôs Backstage. Platform‚Äôs goal is to have at least one new contribution per tribe by the end of September. How to get support? join #hellodev-catalog or email to hellodev-updates@hellofresh.com.

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                              * One big challenge in the infra migration is to remove from the server side anything that conditionally renders different HTML based on the user. We first stopped fetching customer+subscription data from the server, and since this morning we are no longer rendering different experiment variations on the server side. This only affects how we implement logged-out users experiments, since for logged-in users we never had server-side experimentation. The only logged-out user experiment that could be affected has been (Plans page in Factor, not launched yet) refactored to minimize the impact of this architecture change.

üí• Critical Incident

On Tuesday 08/06 the CDN provider Fastly had a major outage, causing Contentful (and half of the internet) to go down. Our website was mostly running ok during the incident (in-memory cache of contentful data), but our mobile apps were crashing for some users. Murtaza from the Mobile Apps team wrote a detailed postmortem of what happened and added action items to prevent another Contentful outage from crashing the apps. Please take some time to read it: https://github.com/hellofresh/post-mortems/tree/20210608-fastly-outage-cause-new-brands-app-crash/20210608-fastly-outage-cause-new-brands-app-crash

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                                    * After some investigations and experiments, Max was able to find one of the big performance bottlenecks in the mobile app (üéâ) : date operations with date-fns. The version we currently use is slow, and when we have components/hooks doing a lot of date calculations the app can become quite slow. After adding memoization to some date operations, the version we had in master became much faster. Because of this, we decided to merge back the BFF changes to master.

                                                                                                                                    * Most of the access control functions have been migrated. Our initial plan to finish this migration this week wasn‚Äôt achieved, since a lot of other more important things came up. Hopefully we will get this done next week.

2021-W13

üõ£Ô∏è Q2+Q3 Roadmap

Solenne, Ahmed, Tobias and I sat down and put our planned projects into a roadmap for Q2 and Q3. Tobias and Solenne presented this roadmap to Yoav and Annie and received good feedback about it. In the second tab of the spreadsheet we listed the priorities, with Porterhouse leading the list. Whenever we have to make a hard choice between two deliveries, we will decide for the one with the higher priority. That makes projects with lower priority more likely to be delayed than the ones with higher priority. If you have any concern of a high-priority project, please let Tobias and Solenne know as soon as possible.

üíª Tech Initiatives

                                                                                                                                    * The BFF migration in the mobile app is almost almost almost complete. We can expect the initiative to be complete early next week. There are still some cleaning up to do on web and mobile.

                                                                                                                                    * Last week we implemented a proof of concept of how we can migrate route access control to react components, and this we started with the migration of the access control function for the Cancellation page. By the end of next week, we should have also migrated the Delivery Tracking and RaF routes.

üí∏ Additional Vouchers

One of Engagement's sprint goals is to support Additional Vouchers in our price calculation logic for web and mobile. This week we started working on the website, refactoring the voucher Redux logic (üçù) and implementing the action to fetch a subscription's additional voucher info.

üî™ Killing Alice

This week we removed the last API call to Alice: update payment method in web. Before Alice is really killed in Intfood (expected mid April), we will need to do a force update of our mobile app to prevent users from using old versions that are still using the old endpoints.

üõí Add-ons

The Happiness team started to implement some changes for Add-Ons, and was able to setup some add-ons SKUs in staging.

### DOC: Nikita / Prateek (Deep Dive) - 2025/12/05 13:04 CET - Notes by Gemini
ID: 1ZrH9rh9OO4FWLwVYdzufa3KLqOQroasXNlOYRhiHiWk

Ôªøüìù Notes

Dec 5, 2025

Nikita / Prateek (Deep Dive)

Invited Nikita Gorshkov Prateek Jajoo

Attachments Nikita / Prateek (Deep Dive) 

Meeting records Recording 





Summary

Nikita Gorshkov and Prateek Jajoo discussed content strategy and app development, acknowledging a weak history in content but recognizing the potential of an app to measure and communicate pet health improvements to users, with the goal of improving social proof and retention. They agreed on the need to define the smallest possible product and to test ideas by understanding pet owners' top worries through a survey, which Nikita Gorshkov confirmed the commercial team can easily incorporate into existing surveys. Prateek Jajoo inquired about the power user demographics, whom Nikita Gorshkov identified as "dinks" in metro areas, with high annual spending on their pets.





Details

Notes Length: Standard

* Content Strategy and App Development Nikita Gorshkov noted the company's weak history in content strategies and daily active user increases, which makes them cautious about investing heavily in content, despite recognizing the interest. They suggested finding easy ways to show users that their products improve pet health, which can then be used as social proof on the website. Prateek Jajoo connected this idea to the potential basis for a pet app, which Nikita Gorshkov affirmed could be a strong idea.

* Testing Ideas and Customer Concerns Nikita Gorshkov emphasized the need to define the smallest possible product and, more importantly, to test interesting ideas to build confidence before committing significant resources. Prateek Jajoo suggested understanding the top five worries or thoughts a pet owner has about their pet to ensure that any app features or solutions address what customers truly care about, thus driving daily usage and engagement. Nikita Gorshkov agreed that providing basic tracking capabilities should be offered not only to active customers but potentially to any pet owners who download the app.

* Surveying Pet Owners To understand customer thoughts, Prateek Jajoo suggested running a survey. Nikita Gorshkov confirmed that the commercial team already runs a survey every two weeks or monthly, and it would be easy to add additional questions due to a good response rate. They shared the contact of Lindsay within the TPT team, who typically runs these in-depth surveys, and offered to add Prateek Jajoo for visibility, mentioning that the latest one they had access to was from August.

* Target Customer Demographics and Spending Prateek Jajoo inquired about the demographics of the power user customer. Nikita Gorshkov identified the power users as "dinks" (Dual Income, No Kids) in metro areas, who have the time, energy, and desire to pamper their pets with fresh frozen food, considering the increase in dog ownership and the perception of pets as children. Nikita Gorshkov noted that the average spend in the US per dog is $1.6k per year, emphasizing that this is a lot of money and the highest amount globally.

* Customer Connection and Health Measurement Prateek Jajoo discussed the emotional attachment and time spent with a dog, suggesting owners would notice improvements in health or appearance, but proposed that the company should help measure and communicate those improvements rather than waiting for the customer to figure it out. Nikita Gorshkov agreed with the sentiment and suggested that Prateek Jajoo speak with Yara, who owns a dog named Boba and represents a good middle ground for their target audience, as she ensures their pet is healthy and happy. Prateek Jajoo connected this idea of measuring and communicating health improvements to solving the retention problem, comparing it to the high utility of services like Amazon Prime.

* Next Steps and Design Bandwidth Prateek Jajoo stated that they would start working on the login page and write a one-pager for review to plan stage one and stage two for a quick win within one sprint. Prateek Jajoo expressed concern about Katrina's bandwidth for the design work. Nikita Gorshkov confirmed they are working to ensure Katrina has the necessary bandwidth and is pushing back on distractions from their senior director.





Suggested next steps

* Prateek Jajoo will start work on the login page and write a one-pager to review and make stage one and stage two plans for a quick win within one sprint.

* Nikita Gorshkov will help Prateek Jajoo navigate where to find the survey and related information by sending the contact for Lindsay and adding Prateek Jajoo to the TPT team for visibility on the surveys.

* Prateek Jajoo will work with the designer Katrina to ensure the right questions are being asked in the survey to get the right information.

* Nikita Gorshkov will ensure that Katrina has the bandwidth for the design work.
